<Text>Bartlett's is a trip back in time to the 50's with a small town market that has a bit of everything. All is good, it costs a bit more, and it is a good deal when you consider travel time and convenience. They are real down home here and polite and kind. The vegetables we looking OK, not a huge selection, but again enough to make a wonderful meal. A good time for all. Smile and enjoy you time travel. What Fun!<//Text>< Rate>

< Text>
Good selection of convenience basics and some grocery (even quality health options!), priced on the high end of fair, probably because of the remote area. Definitely best option in the area for most quick necessities & lite shopping. Dustin is the best clerk year after year. Try the locally made soap at the register... Beautiful and oh so fragrant- A perfect gift</Text>

The new paint job looks great! The owners and employees who work here are generally pleasant and helpful. the cheeses from Petaluma and the local sausage are really delicious. They even have Annie's organic brand products and a great selection of spices. Such a comprehensive selection of products in a relatively small space. Overall a great place!</text>

<Text>Extremely happy with my experience at this place! I came here for my birthday on 3/22/21, and I was pleasantly surprised with the flavor, presentation, and homely vibe at this location. Highly recommend for anyone vegetarian or vegan (even gluten-free)! My sister, a long term vegetarian, said it was the first time she was able to enjoy the fancy sushi. Myself, having recently turned vegetarian, also enjoyed the sushi very much and it more than hit the spot I was craving! We loved it! Don't mistake the name, their sushi is as unique and amazing as their ramen. Vegan sushi is hard to come by and this place does it very well!
Favorite dishes: Pineapple Ramen, Eggplant Roll</Text>< username>

<review>Ordered takeout tonight and it was wonderful. I've been wanting to try their food for a while and it exceeded my expectations.

The food is unique, flavorful, filling, and each dish is a generous portion for the price. My eyes were bigger than my stomach and I had plenty of leftovers for lunch.

Customer service was very kind, though the staff felt frazzled as it was quite busy at 7pm on a Friday. There seemed to be a bunch of takeout orders and there were at least 4 full tables (it's a small place so this was 3/4 full).

There is indoor and outdoor dining on the patio, plus lots of signs about their COVID policies.

I went through their menu, photos, and Yelp reviews to help me narrow down what to order because it was hard to decide.

The Fried Spicy Crispy Tofu was super flavorful though not very crispy (maybe because of takeout)

Tempura Vegan Shrimp Roll (wonderful)

Popcorn Vegan Roll (huge portion, very filling and flavorful)

Kabocha Rice (delicious and feels healing like a macrobiotic dish)

Next time I'd like to try the Spicy Tuna Roll and Mushroom Ramen (or any ramen) as those were highly rated.

The food was gorgeous. Didn't take photos because I was too hungry and ate in my car!

It was easy to find street parking, many street spots on a Friday, and signage was unclear if there are spots for the restaurant in the lots.<//review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPRkhFuyPEhGgmvbCmfAS0Bh2s27lVy1-BbEA16=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO0w41S4YoIfNH0aUeKzGSHomynDQXZtMUuRWoH=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics><resp>None<//resp><gmapID>0x80c2be3959b5d827:0x59bc17910f55cc03<//gmapID></record>

<review>If hell served a beef taco

A lot of people like this place as evidenced by the crowd.  We did not. Now, call us foolish to not order burgers or ice cream at a clearly classic burger/soft serve ice cream joint and compound that with ordering tacos. That said, my fish tacos we're pretty ok and my wife's beef tacos were absolutely the worst either of us have ever had. First she said no onions and they loaded them on both her tacos and side salad. Next, the beef. Oh the beef. If ever the environmental movement needed a clear way to dissuade the world to stop eating beef this would have worked. Overnight cessation of beef eating. Guaranteed. Greasy like crazy and a taste like, hmmm...I think an Amazon box sauteed with Schillings Taco Seasoning would win in side by side taste comparisons. My father who grew up with dire food shortages in Korea drilled into us to eat every grain of rice on our plates, a rule I mostly still follow and respect. I fully supported my wife stopping at bite three or so. I tried one bite and out of sheer awe tried one more.  I did the honors of tossing them as Jolly Kone was already closed by this moment of post prandial trauma. I don't so lightly slam a business nor another's cooking though judging by the crowds and online reviews my petty feedback will not damage business. But if you value and respect to any degree the art form that is the beef taco, I highly recommend that you pass on Tasty Kone's version.< /review><Time>1532820303192< /Time><Name>Bill Say</Name><rating>2</rating><response>None< /response>< userid>

< Review>
Warning:  They use PA's (physicians assistant) not MD's!   If you go here you will most likely not be seen by a medical doctor!

I live in Irvine and usually go to a different urgent care.  I have a PPO insurance so I can go to any urgent care or doctor I choose, who accepts my insurance (Anthem). This one is normally for people who only have HMO as their insurance.  However I'd been here before and due to their longer hours I chose here first thing on a Sunday 7am because I knew I'd be seen right away, rather than other urgent care that isn't open until 9 or 10am.

I was having persistent headaches along with nausea for the past few days, and as a result also couldn't sleep through the night due to pain and stomach discomfort.  I'd taken some OTC medicine but wasn't helping much. I was already scheduled to have some dental work the following Tuesday but didn't seem to be directly related to my symptoms.  I'd considered going to an emergency room due to the discomfort but didn't feel like I was in serious distress and couldn't spend at least $200 to be seen by an MD there.

Instead I went here.   I was seen relatively quickly by a nurse and then the PA came in.  I told him all my symptoms and recent history.  At that point he said, well what do you think is wrong?   Don't know that's why I am here!!  He said hmm, mmm-hmm well we'll get you something for the pain (maybe treating the symptom might help short term but what about the cause... isn't that Med School 101?).  A nurse came in and gave me an injection for pain.  This slightly helped, but my symptoms still persisted after this time and it took weeks for me to just start to feel better.  I should've just gone to the ER or my usual dr/urgent care in the first place.  I also got a bill for $65 in the mail after paying my $20 copay.  I'd have much preferred a prescription if this was going to be the extra cost unbeknownst to me...</Review>

Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada, a saintly little old Indian gentleman who offered to the countercultural youth of the times something which was quite a novelty, someone over 30 in whose guidance they felt that they could  trust. Indeed his
offering of an alternative lifestyle to that of remaining a member of a society gone mad with materialism and militarism or the life of just a social drop out proved quite attractive and the Hare Krsnas as they were called, quickly grew from a small storefront in the Bowery to an International society with centers worldwide. They follow a paradigm that had long held sway over the Western world but which had been rejected during the Enlightenment, a paradigm driven by the notion of a God centered society, in this case centered around the highest Theistic conception of Deity, the divine couple, in the forms a beautiful, youthful, playful God, Lord Krsna and Srimati Radharani.
The temple is in the heart of the city near to the beach.  The God forms on display are installed with a practice of Theurgy long forgotten in the West that invests them with the presence of Godhead itself, which, if you are sensitive, you may even feel, hear or see come alive before you. Even if you donâ€™t though, simply seeing them is considered to be spiritually uplifting and if you are just looking for some novelty or to broaden your cultural horizon there is that too.
The â€˜devoteesâ€™ as members of this faith are called follow an ascetic discipline meant to reign in the senses and control the mind in order to reduce disturbances and to gain self mastery that they might apply themselves without deviation towards their principle practice of Bhakti yoga which is distinct from Patanjalis system though it includes liberation as a secondary focus.
Subhadra dd, the last and only devotee I ever introduced into this movement following its founders death, was part of this temple community many years ago and has some favorable memories of it and we still visit it together once in a while as the deities are very dear to her and her positive experiences here were formative of the love for Krsna that her devotional service developed during her years within the International Society for Krsna Consciousness.  Krsna protected her, which I had hoped He would do, especially since it was He that arranged the introduction. Many years later Krsna brought her and her back into my life shortly after the death of a loved one had removed from my life all purpose and meaning. Though I have never been a member of this faith, neither Krsna, nor His devotees seem to hold that against me and this was not the first time that my soul had been restored by this beautiful blue God and His even more merciful devotees. The food is both tasty and holy, since it is offered to Krsna before it is served. Donâ€™t however count the calories, especially if you stop by at their Sunday feast.
The temple attracts a lot of Hindus and their really nice people,  on-judgemental, respectful, open and welcoming. I used to sit around and chat with the old timers who remembered the Raj, Gandhi, so much  and about their views on things.
The predominant world views foundational doctrine asserts, in the  words of John Locke, that â€œGod is unknowable by definition.â€ This religion teaches that through love that God may be known. There was a time in my life in which an acceptance of either one of those contradictory claims would have been for me a matter of blind faith acceptance, but that time in my life was before I came into contact with this society and its founder A.C.Bhaktivedanta Swami Srila Prabhupada who the Beatles, especially George Harrison were also very fond of.</text>

< review>
My fiancÃ© and I were planning on having a nice night out. We've been going through a lot and really needed it. I talked about Straits and told him how amazing it was and really talked it up. We got to the outside lounge and the host said we could stay for about an hour before bottle service. We got to our seats and she served us water. < Review>
An "oldie but a goodie" on Santana Row. In the before times it was a great venue for birthday parties and private events, now it's a great spot for outdoor dining. The patio on the side has heat lamps overhead to keep diners comfortable. The tables on the street has freestanding heat lamps.
Service can be a bit slow to start but once food is ordered it shows up quickly, fresh, and hot.
Sushi sampler was the one disappointing dish - nothing bad, but nothing special.
Shaking Beef was better than I remembered with perfect medium rare steak. Lobster tail garlic noodles was delightful.
Drinks are beautifully made. Highly recommended for a nice dinner out.<//Review>

Pros:
- Food was great, decent portions for the price
- ambiance is awesome, feels like sitting right on Santana Row.

Cons:
- terribly understaffed
- orders weren't just right. We asked for no straws in our drinks, and we got straws. We asked for extra spicy entrees and they were mild.

It took forever for us to get our checks and that really soured our mood, but those hostesses were doing all they could. The orders being off is probably a result of how understaffed they were.

Great location right along Santana Row

If you arrive just before dinner time, you can easily get seated. The hostesses were very accommodating with my need to work and eat and plug in my laptop. They seated me in an area where I could do my phone calls and work while I ate. The menu is different if you are seated at the lounge vs the dining area and drinks are different prices too.

Menu selection is great in both the dining area and lounge. Lots of exotic dishes that is a fusion of American and Asian cuisine. Prices arenâ€™t too bad with a lot of entrÃ©e dishes under $30. Beverage selection is pretty good and prices are average. The portions are a little on the small side but very tasty. Service was good from the time you are seated to the time you finish off. They didnâ€™t have any issues with me moving about the restaurant and changing tables.

It gets a little loud as the night progresses because of the music and a different crowd encroaches. It seems like a usual hangout for business visitors though.

I ordered the Pan Seared Salmon for $20. It was really unique with all my favourite flavours mixed in from cilantro to lemongrass chili sambal and mango salsa sauce. Salmon was done perfectly. I would go back again but the only unfortunate thing about Santana Row is that most of the restaurants are closed by around 11pm.</text>

< text>
Unlike the Straits in San Francisco, this location has an outdoor patio with heaters - perfect to stay nice and toasty during the chilly bay area nights.

We have dined on the banana blossom salad, chicken satay, roti, chicken lollipops, banana leaf salmon, butter chicken, mee goreng, and a few other dishes. Everything is delicious, but can be on the greasy side and can also sometimes vary in consistency. Nothing a nice cocktail cannot wash down, I assume.

The weekends can get crowded, so be sure to make reservations.< /text>

<Text>BEWARE Please post if you have been victimized at a Straits Restaurant :
I was a patron in Straits restaurant on the evening of December 19, 2013, following a shopping trip in Santana Row. My boyfriend and I stopped in to have dinner and drinks in your bar.  I inquired to the bartender that my phone was dying and was there a convenient location for me to charge it while we ate. He kindly stated he could charge it behind the bar securely next to the cashwrap.

When we went to retrieve the phone after leaving, we were handed back ONLY the charger, not the phone.  This was a brand new Iphone 5S with 2 months worth of data and content backed up over a 9 year period.

We spoke with the MOD, the bartender and were informed that security cameras could identify the culprit, although that was never done.  Instead we were told to wait until the next day when we would be contacted again by the MOD, Jonathon Young.

We contacted Jonathon the next day and he assured us he would take care of the matter and that we would be reimbursed for the phone since it was clearly stolen from one of your employees. (The bar area is supposed to be secure with only the bartender and bar back entering the secured area.)

Several emails to Mr. Young proved unfruitful. I finally received a phone call from Heather Conry, on January 8. I called her back the same day and left a message as I was traveling.  I called her back again and again, and my boyfriend also called left her repeated messages.  She likely has over 6 messages between us.  It's unconscionable to me why she would reach out initially and then have ZERO follow through.  Im not sure what kind of management team you are running there, but it's unacceptable behavior.

We are considering opting into social media to spread the word of the poor service and treatment you have of your patrons.

Is this how you run a successful customer oriented restaurant ?</Text>< user_id>
